  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3456757219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3456757219" />
    <a title="Di Maitland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland"><img alt="Di Maitland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585661189p2/112155925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3456757219?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Di Maitland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Di Maitland" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland">Di Maitland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671654160" href="/book/show/1559985.Sheepfarmer_s_Daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=action-girl">action-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=titled-characters">titled-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=non-humans">non-humans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=swords">swords</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=medieval-setting">medieval-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3456757219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8189855531510394125"><blockquote>I think you have as fine a young warrior as I've seen. That's what I hear, as well, from all who have mentioned her. Too impulsive, perhaps, like most young fighters, but that comes as much from generosity as anything else. I think she'll go beyond a hired fighter in the ranks, if nothing breaks that will or that honesty."</blockquote><br/>A wonderful account of the early years of a hero. Told in an unusual way, it focuses on the nitty gritty realities of life in a mercenary company. At times, this slowed the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText8189855531510394125" style="display:none"><blockquote>I think you have as fine a young warrior as I've seen. That's what I hear, as well, from all who have mentioned her. Too impulsive, perhaps, like most young fighters, but that comes as much from generosity as anything else. I think she'll go beyond a hired fighter in the ranks, if nothing breaks that will or that honesty."</blockquote><br>A wonderful account of the early years of a hero. Told in an unusual way, it focuses on the nitty gritty realities of life in a mercenary company. At times, this slowed the story, but on the whole, I found it made for a more believable journey.<br><br>I first read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96281.The_Deed_of_Paksenarrion__The_Deed_of_Paksenarrion___1_3_" title="The Deed of Paksenarrion (The Deed of Paksenarrion, #1-3) by Elizabeth Moon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deed of Paksenarrion</a> back in 2016, just as I was finishing university. I remember really enjoying it, though getting a little frustrated with the pacing at times. Paks, I remember as a solid, dependable heroine, more interested in a good job well done than heroics and theatrics. Plot-wise, I thought I'd remembered little. It turns out that I'd remembered quite a lot, I'd just misattributed most of it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147843.Green_Rider__Green_Rider___1_" title="Green Rider (Green Rider, #1) by Kristen Britain" rel="nofollow noopener">Green Rider</a> (goodness knows why). Reading it again, it all came flooding back and I was able to focus on the little details and the subtle hints that I'd missed first time around. Having recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1852521.Surrender_None__Legacy_of_Gird___1_" title="Surrender None (Legacy of Gird, #1) by Elizabeth Moon" rel="nofollow noopener">Surrender None</a> for the first time, it was also interesting to compare Paks to Gird, and to see his legacy and how his legend grew after his death. Both books certainly share a fascination for military minutiae and salt of the earth protagonists.<br><br>The book begins with Paks, aged 19 and arranged to be wed, leaving home to join Duke Phelan's mercenary company in Tsaia. Here she comes under the command of Sergeant Stammel who teaches her the ropes: camp etiquette, marching and formations, horse-riding, sword work and so on. She makes friends, but also enemies and readers should note that there is a scene of attempted rape. Soon enough she's marching south, over the Dwarfmounts to Aarenis and her first military encounters.<br><br>Early on, Paks is noted for her hard-work and humble attitude. She's good with a sword but not unrealistically so. Her first truly distinguishing moment comes when she and two friends escape an attack by Siniava, a brutal mercenary leader, and travel seven days cross-country, tracking the enemy and scavenging for food, in order to warn the Duke of an imminent attack. It is also around this time that Paks is given a Girdish amulet which, inexplicably, serves to warn and protect her in times of direst need. Talent and "luck", together with her stolid persona, single Paks out again and again, and no one doubts that great deeds are to come.<br><blockquote>"Something is moving you, which I do not understand, and I think you hardly realise. You may be called to leave your Duke, at least for a time. If so, I hope you will understand the need."</blockquote><br>If Paks is anything, she is real. Smart enough and keen to learn, but not without her naivetés. She sees the world in black and white - good and bad - and wants to fight for one against the other. A natural leader, she cares for those under her command and manages to walk that fine line between approachability and leadership by example. In some distant part of her mind, she dreams of leading a company one day, but, assuming this unachievable, is happy to follow those in command and take her promotions where she's earned them. <br><br>Aside from Paks, my favourite characters were Saben, a fellow recruit and Siniava escapee, and Sergeant Stammel. I appreciated that the friendship that grew between Paks and Saben was allowed to remain just that - a friendship. Paks is asexual - the first asexual character I've ever come across in fiction - and Saben respects her wishes, staying loyally by her side and supporting her at every turn. It makes a refreshing break from the usual romances that come to consume a plot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I almost cried when Saben died on his and Paks' mission to warn the Duke. I had completely forgotten that that happened and was expecting him to return, bumped and bruised, to his rightful place at Paks' side. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Stammel, meanwhile, is something of a father figure to the recruits under him. He knows their ins and outs and trusts them, even when others bring their trust into question. He goes above and beyond his duties to train and nurture his men, ensuring that they can not only fight, but also manage the money they win fighting. And he listens - when times get tough and shit happens, he's there, with a shoulder for you to cry on and soft word that things will be ok.<br><br>Duke Kieri Phelan, himself, also deserves a mention here. Known as the Fox, he runs a respectable company that prides itself on fighting hard but also respecting the rules of combat and dealing fairly with the locals. He welcomes both men and women to the band and they are treated equally. He leads from the front and holds the respect and admiration of his men. He has a temper but works hard to moderate it and isn't afraid to give praise where praise is due. After squiring with Aliam Halveric in his youth, he has ties to other companies and often works with them to better achieve his goals. Some question his right to the title of Duke, but those who matter don't care. This is important later if I remember rightly.<br><br>Characters aside, Paks’ world also includes non-human creatures - though we see little of them in this book - and humans capable of magic. I’d forgotten this from my first read which is odd, on the one hand, considering what a pivotal role magic comes to play, but not so surprising, on the other hand, considering that so few characters are able to wield it. Largely linked to one religion or another, we see magic wielded for good, healing those wounded in battle, and magic wielded for evil, to torture or harm. If I remember rightly, we see a lot more of this in the books to come. On the whole, though, Paks’ world is much like any other pseudo-medieval-European fantasy world with its farms and its forts. Comforting but not hugely inventive.<br><br>If I had to describe the book in one word, it would be <b>SOLID</b>. The characters are realistic and wholesome, steady in their pursuit of their humble goals and slowly but surely transforming into the heroes we know them to be. The plot develops one step at a time and isn’t victim to the extreme emotional highs and lows of many a young adult fantasy book. And the writing is compelling whilst also delving into such detail at times that you feel you could be there, mucking in with the rest of the troops. Definitely recommend for those looking for their next epic fantasy fix.<br><br>If you like Sheepfarmer's Daughter, you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1852521.Surrender_None__Legacy_of_Gird___1_" title="Surrender None (Legacy of Gird, #1) by Elizabeth Moon" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1414174750l/1852521._SY75_.jpg" alt="Surrender None (Legacy of Gird, #1) by Elizabeth Moon" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1515589515l/186074._SX50_.jpg" alt="The Name of the Wind (The Kingkiller Chronicle, #1) by Patrick Rothfuss" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings__The_Stormlight_Archive___1_" title="The Way of Kings (The Stormlight Archive, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer13924158872537422377">...So what does that leave us with. <i>Sheepfarmer's Daughter</i> is essentially five hundred pages of Paks going through the motions of becoming a mercenary and finding out how to be a good soldier, a lot of which is no more interesting that my average day at the office.   <span id="freeText13924158872537422377" style="display:none">...So what does that leave us with. <i>Sheepfarmer's Daughter</i> is essentially five hundred pages of Paks going through the motions of becoming a mercenary and finding out how to be a good soldier, a lot of which is no more interesting that my average day at the office. She does what she is told, never seriously questions what she is doing and turns out to be good at pretty much everything she is required to do. In short, neither Paks, or the events described in the novel really managed captivate me. It is readable but I wouldn't go as far as calling it good.  I understand that <i>Sheepfarmer's Daughter</i> was Moon's first published novel. One can only hope she has improved plotting and characterization since.<br /><br /><a href="http://valsrandomcomments.blogspot.com/2013/05/sheepfarmers-daughter-elizabeth-moon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Random Comments review</a></span>

<div id="review_95297213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95297213" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95297213?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441851185" href="/book/show/7230176-sheepfarmer-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95297213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8710743650096723534">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>Brilliance Audio has recently been putting together some fine productions of many classic fantasy novels that deserve to be heard and I, as a reader, couldn’t be happier. I don’t have much free time these days, and most of my reading is now done by audio, so I was thrilled to find that I could finally listen to The Deed of Paksenarrion by Elizabeth Moon. The first novel, Sheepfarmer’s Daughter, has just been released, and the rest are following quickly. (B</span>
  <span id="freeText8710743650096723534" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />Brilliance Audio has recently been putting together some fine productions of many classic fantasy novels that deserve to be heard and I, as a reader, couldn’t be happier. I don’t have much free time these days, and most of my reading is now done by audio, so I was thrilled to find that I could finally listen to The Deed of Paksenarrion by Elizabeth Moon. The first novel, Sheepfarmer’s Daughter, has just been released, and the rest are following quickly. (By the way, if audiobooks are out of your budget, ask your public library to order them — my library has ordered several that I’ve requested with their online form.)<br /><br />I enjoyed this story about Paksenarrion (Paks) who, to avoid an arranged marriage to a farmer, runs away to join a mercenary force. It’s not that she knows there’s a future Mr. Right out there, or even that she knows there’s some great evil in the land to be vanquished, but rather that she just isn’t interested in being married or being a farmer’s wife. Of course, life as a mercenary isn’t exactly what she expected, but Paks is honest, competent, and hard-working, so she does pretty well at her new job and we can easily foresee that she’s developing into a future leader.<br /><br />I had no trouble believing in any of Moon’s characters or their relationships with each other. It didn’t take long for me to find myself rooting and caring for Paks and I was really affected when some of her friends and allies were injured or killed.<br /><br />Elizabeth Moon’s military experience is evident and she writes believably about the daily minutiae of being a soldier. There’s more time spent marching, eating, waiting, exercising, and being stuck in the mud than fighting. This is very realistic, I’m sure, but it makes the novel move rather slowly at times, and gives it a didactic flavor. I think that readers who haven’t read as many coming-of-age-in-an-army stories as I have will not be so impatient.<br /><br />Jennifer Van Dyck was a terrific reader with a pleasant voice which effectively portrayed both men and women. There were times when I didn’t care for the over-eager wide-eyed country girl voice that she used for Paks (couldn’t a few of those Yes, Sirs been a little less enthusiastic?), but it’s hard to tell if that was her interpretation or the author’s intent. Overall, Ms. Van Dyck is a reader I’ll be watching for in the future, and Paksenarrion, the sheepfarmer’s daughter, is a heroine whose story I’m looking forward to hearing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8710743650096723534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18814678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18814678" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/627337-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261273615p2/627337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18814678?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/627337-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=z2011-reads">z2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=sff-fantasy">sff-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18814678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11977231204063582018">I was reading the newest book in the Paks series,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7852732.Oath_of_Fealty' title='Oath of Fealty by Elizabeth Moon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Oath of Fealty</a> and it made me very nostalgic to go back and re-read this.<br/><br/>I read this book for the first time back in 1994, I think it was. Some friends and I were holidaying up along the east coast and we stopped in Martha's Vineyard. There is a really cool Hostel there in the middle of the woods (the outdoor shower is awesome!). I didn't want to carry too many books around so I'd only had a couple on me and was being stingy about how much I was r</span>
  <span id="freeText11977231204063582018" style="display:none">I was reading the newest book in the Paks series,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7852732.Oath_of_Fealty" title="Oath of Fealty by Elizabeth Moon" rel="nofollow noopener">Oath of Fealty</a> and it made me very nostalgic to go back and re-read this.<br /><br />I read this book for the first time back in 1994, I think it was. Some friends and I were holidaying up along the east coast and we stopped in Martha's Vineyard. There is a really cool Hostel there in the middle of the woods (the outdoor shower is awesome!). I didn't want to carry too many books around so I'd only had a couple on me and was being stingy about how much I was reading, parcelling out a few pages here and there (man, what i wouldn't have done for an e-reader back then!) <br /><br />At the Hostel they had a bookshelf and they encouraged people to leave/take books. This book was on the shelf and I sat down and started to read it. And was instantly transported.<br /><br />Paks is a Sheepfarmer's daughter who didn't want to marry the Pig farmer her father had dowered her to. With the stories of glory and fighting that her cousin had told them about being a soldier ringing in her ears, Paks runs away and joins the Duke Phelan's Mercenary company.<br /><br />This book is military high fantasy in it's best form. There are great scenes of training, learning, fighting and soldierly camaraderie. There is also magical peril and a great, major big evil that the company fight against. In the meantime, Paks makes friends, loses friends, and becomes a good soldier who manages to stand out in ways she would have never considered.<br /><br />I finished the book that night, and was bereft because I knew there was a second book but it wasn't anywhere on that shelf. Darnit. The minute, I could, I got the second book.<br /><br />Thus began my love affair with the Paks series. I think over the years, I've read the trilogy about three times. They never get old and still feel like I am reading them new again. Great book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11977231204063582018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_181406051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181406051" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4367251-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303001337p2/4367251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181406051?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/4367251-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367251-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181406051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3149836796647089020">The first book in the Deed of Paksenarrion series (One noun, five sylables, instant red alert).<br/><br/>I have to preface this by saying that I found Lord of the Ring's unbearably tedious, and that every time I read -or try to- 80's fantasy (Wheel of Time in particular) I am struck by a profound sadness that Tolkien's ludicrous Middle-England populated by gay midgets, gay elves and gay... men became the template rather than Le Guin's Earthsea.<br/><br/>Sheepfarmer's Daughter really is eighties fantasy. A girl with</span>
  <span id="freeText3149836796647089020" style="display:none">The first book in the Deed of Paksenarrion series (One noun, five sylables, instant red alert).<br /><br />I have to preface this by saying that I found Lord of the Ring's unbearably tedious, and that every time I read -or try to- 80's fantasy (Wheel of Time in particular) I am struck by a profound sadness that Tolkien's ludicrous Middle-England populated by gay midgets, gay elves and gay... men became the template rather than Le Guin's Earthsea.<br /><br />Sheepfarmer's Daughter really is eighties fantasy. A girl with a name longer than her hair (Paksenarrion Dorthansdotter) runs away from home (and an arranged marriage!) to become a Protagonist. In a world of magic swords, elves, dwarves, orcs and all the rest of the gubbins that screams "I played D&amp;D and can recite Fellowship word for word". However, despite the fact that every red flag is raised to skyscraper height, it's really good. In spite of all the nonsense. It may even be good <i>because</i> of all the nonsense.<br /><br />The novel has been carved from archetype and Dungeons &amp; Dragons source books but because it knows this and plays it so unflinchingly straight -also likely because this is revealed piecemeal alongside a really compelling narrative- I found myself willingly led along. I also really appreciate a book that's brave enough to tell a story from the front line perspective and keep it there. Long stretches of Paks experience involve standing watch, securing horse food and marching places, short stretches involve trying to avoid getting stabbed and tiny flashes involve her witnessing magical and otherworldly activities. Which confuse her as much as they do us.<br /> <br />To be negative for a moment, the characters that aren't Paksenarrion are mostly shoddily drawn up until the last few chapters. This is a real shame as The Halveric's Son Point of View chapter was intensely moving, and if she is <i>able</i> to do that with her characters then why are so many of Paks fellows such ciphers? Also a sizable section (10%) of the book is a very boring odyssey from one fortified position to another, rendered devoid of tension by the poor characterisation.<br /><br />These foibles aside, though, it's a very competent work with some interesting blurring of the moral spectrum in the last chapter and is piled high all the way through with confident and unhurried foreshadowing.<br /><br />Really a solid, professional fantasy work all around, and a pleasure to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3149836796647089020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_616902407" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/616902407" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/616902407?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer616902407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer633076527690501283">I wanted to like this book, but it just did not work (for me). <br/><br/>Although the writing is thorough and descriptive, most of the problems I have with this book come down to its third person (sort of) limited narration. Most of the time, details enhance the story and help build the world, but sometimes they're repetitive and yet you still don't get to know much about the world the story is set in. The latter applies to this story. There are a few scenes where magic played an important role <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoi</a></span>
  <span id="freeText633076527690501283" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book, but it just did not work (for me). <br /><br />Although the writing is thorough and descriptive, most of the problems I have with this book come down to its third person (sort of) limited narration. Most of the time, details enhance the story and help build the world, but sometimes they're repetitive and yet you still don't get to know much about the world the story is set in. The latter applies to this story. There are a few scenes where magic played an important role <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like the Honey Cat's capture or Paks' mysterious pendant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but you don't find out how magic system(s) work, not because it can't be explained, but because the main character doesn't know herself.<br /><br />Another thing that kept me from getting into this story was the characters and how interchangeable they were. They had no personality or personal traits to separate one character from another. Paks, as a main character, as a lowly soldier in the ranks, doesn't know much of anything, let alone important things, like magic. So the reader just has to accept these things, without explanation, as they happen. But I suppose that's the whole point since Elizabeth Moon wanted to write a story from the POV of a soldier.<br /><br />If it weren't for all the violence and gore that she has to experience, Paks would fit the Mary Sue mold very well. Things just happen to her and she reacts to them, in an appropriate manner or whatever that's appropriate for the situation. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A supernatural force just happens to take a liking to her and saves her from death multiple times. NBD. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I know all of these issues can easily be resolved by my reading the rest of the trilogy since Elizabeth Moon wrote the series as one book. And I'll get around to it... eventually.</span>
  <a data-text-id="633076527690501283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_108758203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108758203" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108758203?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/6434207-sheepfarmer-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=swords-and-sorcery">swords-and-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=secondary-world">secondary-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=female-protagonist">female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=fantasy-medieval">fantasy-medieval</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108758203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12196086570004600810">This is an off-the-shelf AD&D adventure, with the names (barely) filed off. If you like that sort of thing, it's a decent story and Elizabeth Moon's writing is better than average. But it's basically about a sheepfarmer's daughter (duh) who joins a mercenary company and becomes a fighter, and the whole book is about her training and her first few military campaigns. There's only a little bit of magic, but it's obvious Paksenarrion is destined to become a paladin. Although I'm slightly curious to</span>
  <span id="freeText12196086570004600810" style="display:none">This is an off-the-shelf AD&amp;D adventure, with the names (barely) filed off. If you like that sort of thing, it's a decent story and Elizabeth Moon's writing is better than average. But it's basically about a sheepfarmer's daughter (duh) who joins a mercenary company and becomes a fighter, and the whole book is about her training and her first few military campaigns. There's only a little bit of magic, but it's obvious Paksenarrion is destined to become a paladin. Although I'm slightly curious to see how she progresses, it's kind of the same curiosity that makes you want to keep playing an RPG with a character who's just numbers on paper to you -- it would be nice to see her level up and acquire some new abilities, but there's no real emotional investment in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12196086570004600810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I6e1vk3Ro/64EADuSY8C0brQ6cCLwEJaMePL0OyEtt10RrGPslzafNydFWc4P8q8GaqXcT2zeoLWBUzGrn+giw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c5HatOlORJN/awofBH3uPiBq7LI4+4qv0y8TVES9oOskcN6FFsM9ERvmH5Z1zSZTgxCSA46Isnc0yZRCBka2vQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5665535600339553234">Elizabeth Moon was born March 7, 1945, and grew up in McAllen, Texas, graduating from McAllen High School in 1963. She has a B.A. in History from Rice University (1968) and another in Biology from the University of Texas at Austin (1975) with graduate work in Biology at the University of Texas, San Antonio.<br/><br/>She served in the USMC from 1968 to 1971, first at MCB Quantico and then at HQMC. She marrie</span>
  <span id="freeText5665535600339553234" style="display:none">Elizabeth Moon was born March 7, 1945, and grew up in McAllen, Texas, graduating from McAllen High School in 1963. She has a B.A. in History from Rice University (1968) and another in Biology from the University of Texas at Austin (1975) with graduate work in Biology at the University of Texas, San Antonio.<br /><br />She served in the USMC from 1968 to 1971, first at MCB Quantico and then at HQMC. She married Richard Moon, a Rice classmate and Army officer, in 1969; they moved to the small central Texas town where they still live in 1979. They have one son, born in 1983. <br /><br />She started writing stories and poems as a small child; attempted first book (an illustrated biography of the family dog) at age six. Started writing science fiction in high school, but considered writing merely a sideline. First got serious about writing (as in, submitting things and actually getting money...) in the 1980s. Made first fiction sale at age forty--"Bargains" to Marion Zimmer Bradley's Sword &amp; Sorceress III and "ABCs in Zero G" to Analog. Her first novel, <i>Sheepfarmer's Daughter</i>, sold in 1987 and came out in 1988; it won the Compton Crook Award in 1989. <i>Remnant Population</i> was a Hugo nominee in 1997, and <i>The Speed of Dark</i> was a finalist for the Arthur C. Clarke Award, and won the Nebula in 2004.</span>
